## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of concentration dA/dt as a function of concentration A and time t, which is the fundamental problem in chemical kinetics. The rate law typically depends on powers of concentration, and time-dependence may arise from catalytic deactivation, photochemical forcing, or complex multi-step mechanisms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to square of concentration)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate law)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (combination of first and second order)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme/saturation kinetics)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (product-catalyzed reaction)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse reaction with equilibrium)
- Langmuir-Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (surface-catalyzed reaction kinetics)
- Time-dependent decay rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (rate with catalyst deactivation or activation)
- Fractional order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (generalized rate with constant source/sink)
- Competitive inhibition: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2) (substrate inhibition kinetics)
- Power-law with time modulation: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * t**c2 (diffusion-limited or aging kinetics)
- Sigmoidal rate: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (cooperative/Hill-type kinetics)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Negative rate values (consumption) with magnitude increasing with concentration → simple power-law rate law dA_dt = -k * A^n
- Rate approaching zero at both low and high concentrations → saturation kinetics with substrate inhibition (rational function with A^2 in denominator)
- Rate that changes sign at a specific concentration → reversible reaction with equilibrium concentration (linear: c0*A + c1 where c1 > 0, c0 < 0)
- Rate proportional to A*(constant - A) → autocatalytic or logistic-type reaction where product catalyzes the reaction
- Explicit time dependence in rate law beyond what A(t) provides → catalyst deactivation, photochemical forcing, or diffusion-limited kinetics
- Rate with non-integer apparent order → complex multi-step mechanism or fractal kinetics in heterogeneous media
- Rate that plateaus at high concentration → enzyme saturation or surface site limitation (Michaelis-Menten form)
- Log-linear relationship between rate and concentration → integer-order kinetics (slope gives reaction order)
